### Explanation:
- **Django**: The web framework used for building the backend of the application.
- **djangorestframework**: A powerful toolkit for building Web APIs in Django.
- **mysqlclient**: A MySQL database adapter for Python, required for connecting Django to a MySQL database.
- **django-cors-headers**: A Django app for handling the server headers required for Cross-Origin Resource Sharing (CORS).
- **djangorestframework-simplejwt**: A JSON Web Token authentication plugin for Django REST Framework.
- **react**: The JavaScript library used for building the frontend components.
- **axios**: A promise-based HTTP client for the browser and Node.js, used for making HTTP requests from the React components.

"models.py
```python
'''
Defines the database models for the accounting system.
'''
from django.db import models
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
class Account(models.Model):
    name = models.CharField(max_length=255)
    balance = models.DecimalField(max_digits=10, decimal_places=2)
class Invoice(models.Model):
    account = models.ForeignKey(Account, on_delete=models.CASCADE)
    amount = models.DecimalField(max_digits=10, decimal_places=2)
    date = models.DateField()
class Purchase(models.Model):
    item = models.CharField(max_length=255)
    amount = models.DecimalField(max_digits=10, decimal_places=2)
    date = models.DateField()
class InventoryItem(models.Model):
    name = models.CharField(max_length=255)
    quantity = models.IntegerField()
class FinancialReport(models.Model):
    title = models.CharField(max_length=255)
    content = models.TextField()
class UserRole(models.Model):
    user = models.ForeignKey(User, on_delete=models.CASCADE)
    role_name = models.CharField(max_length=255)
```
views.py
```python
'''
Handles HTTP requests and responses for the accounting system.
'''
from django.shortcuts import render
from rest_framework import viewsets, permissions
from .models import Account, Invoice, Purchase, InventoryItem, FinancialReport, UserRole
from .serializers import AccountSerializer, InvoiceSerializer, PurchaseSerializer, InventoryItemSerializer, FinancialReportSerializer, UserRoleSerializer
from rest_framework.permissions import BasePermission
class IsAccountManager(BasePermission):
    def has_permission(self, request, view):
        return request.user.userrole_set.filter(role_name='Account Manager').exists()
class IsInvoiceManager(BasePermission):
    def has_permission(self, request, view):
        return request.user.userrole_set.filter(role_name='Invoice Manager').exists()
class IsPurchaseManager(BasePermission):
    def has_permission(self, request, view):
        return request.user.userrole_set.filter(role_name='Purchase Manager').exists()
class IsInventoryManager(BasePermission):
    def has_permission(self, request, view):
        return request.user.userrole_set.filter(role_name='Inventory Manager').exists()
class IsReportManager(BasePermission):
    def has_permission(self, request, view):
        return request.user.userrole_set.filter(role_name='Report Manager').exists()
class AccountViewSet(viewsets.ModelViewSet):
    queryset = Account.objects.all()
    serializer_class = AccountSerializer
    permission_classes = [permissions.IsAuthenticated, IsAccountManager]
class InvoiceViewSet(viewsets.ModelViewSet):
    queryset = Invoice.objects.all()
    serializer_class = InvoiceSerializer
    permission_classes = [permissions.IsAuthenticated, IsInvoiceManager]
class PurchaseViewSet(viewsets.ModelViewSet):
    queryset = Purchase.objects.all()
    serializer_class = PurchaseSerializer
    permission_classes = [permissions.IsAuthenticated, IsPurchaseManager]
class InventoryItemViewSet(viewsets.ModelViewSet):
    queryset = InventoryItem.objects.all()
    serializer_class = InventoryItemSerializer
    permission_classes = [permissions.IsAuthenticated, IsInventoryManager]
class FinancialReportViewSet(viewsets.ModelViewSet):
    queryset = FinancialReport.objects.all()
    serializer_class = FinancialReportSerializer
    permission_classes = [permissions.IsAuthenticated, IsReportManager]
class UserRoleViewSet(viewsets.ModelViewSet):
    queryset = UserRole.objects.all()
    serializer_class = UserRoleSerializer
    permission_classes = [permissions.IsAuthenticated]
```
serializers.py
```python
'''
Serializes the models for the accounting system.
'''
from rest_framework import serializers
from .models import Account, Invoice, Purchase, InventoryItem, FinancialReport, UserRole
class AccountSerializer(serializers.ModelSerializer):
    class Meta:
        model = Account
        fields = '__all__'
class InvoiceSerializer(serializers.ModelSerializer):
    class Meta:
        model = Invoice
        fields = '__all__'
class PurchaseSerializer(serializers.ModelSerializer):
    class Meta:
        model = Purchase
        fields = '__all__'
class InventoryItemSerializer(serializers.ModelSerializer):
    class Meta:
        model = InventoryItem
        fields = '__all__'
class FinancialReportSerializer(serializers.ModelSerializer):
    class Meta:
        model = FinancialReport
        fields = '__all__'
class UserRoleSerializer(serializers.ModelSerializer):
    class Meta:
        model = UserRole
        fields = '__all__'
```

urls.py
```python
'''
Defines URL routing for the accounting system.
'''
from django.urls import path, include
from rest_framework.routers import DefaultRouter
from .views import AccountViewSet, InvoiceViewSet, PurchaseViewSet, InventoryItemViewSet, FinancialReportViewSet, UserRoleViewSet
router = DefaultRouter()
router.register(r'accounts', AccountViewSet)
router.register(r'invoices', InvoiceViewSet)
router.register(r'purchases', PurchaseViewSet)
router.register(r'inventory', InventoryItemViewSet)
router.register(r'reports', FinancialReportViewSet)
router.register(r'userroles', UserRoleViewSet)
urlpatterns = [
    path('', include(router.urls)),
]
```
app.js
```js
'''
Main entry point for the React application.
'''
import React from 'react';
import { BrowserRouter as Router, Route, Switch } from 'react-router-dom';
import AccountComponent from './components/AccountComponent';
import InvoiceComponent from './components/InvoiceComponent';
import PurchaseComponent from './components/PurchaseComponent';
import InventoryComponent from './components/InventoryComponent';
import ReportComponent from './components/ReportComponent';
import UserRoleComponent from './components/UserRoleComponent';
function App() {
  return (
    <Router>
      <Switch>
        <Route path="/accounts" component={AccountComponent} />
        <Route path="/invoices" component={InvoiceComponent} />
        <Route path="/purchases" component={PurchaseComponent} />
        <Route path="/inventory" component={InventoryComponent} />
        <Route path="/reports" component={ReportComponent} />
        <Route path="/userroles" component={UserRoleComponent} />
      </Switch>
    </Router>
  );
}
export default App;
```
accountcomponent.js
```js
'''
Component for managing accounts.
'''
import React, { useState, useEffect } from 'react';
import axios from 'axios';
function AccountComponent() {
  const [accounts, setAccounts] = useState([]);
  useEffect(() => {
    axios.get('/api/accounts/')
      .then(response => setAccounts(response.data))
      .catch(error => console.error('Error fetching accounts:', error));
  }, []);
  return (
    <div>
      <h1>Accounts</h1>
      <ul>
        {accounts.map(account => (
          <li key={account.id}>{account.name}: {account.balance}</li>
        ))}
      </ul>
    </div>
  );
}
export default AccountComponent;
```

```js
function InvoiceComponent() {
```

```js
import React, { useState, useEffect } from 'react';
import axios from 'axios';
function ReportComponent() {
  const [reports, setReports] = useState([]);
  useEffect(() => {
    axios.get('/api/reports/')
      .then(response => setReports(response.data))
      .catch(error => console.error('Error fetching reports:', error));
  }, []);
  return (
    <div>
      <h1>Financial Reports</h1>
      <ul>
        {reports.map(report => (
          <li key={report.id}>{report.title}</li>
        ))}
      </ul>
    </div>
  );
}
```

```js
'''
Component for managing user roles.

import React, { useState, useEffect } from 'react';
import axios from 'axios';
function UserRoleComponent() {
  const [roles, setRoles] = useState([]);
  useEffect(() => {
    axios.get('/api/userroles/')
      .then(response => setRoles(response.data))
      .catch(error => console.error('Error fetching user roles:', error));
  }, []);
  return (
    <div>
      <h1>User Roles</h1>
      <ul>
        {roles.map(role => (
          <li key={role.id}>{role.role_name}</li>
        ))}
      </ul>
    </div>
  );
}
export default UserRoleComponent;
```

"models.py
```python
'''
Defines the database models for the accounting system.
'''
from django.db import models
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
class Account(models.Model):
    name = models.CharField(max_length=255)
    balance = models.DecimalField(max_digits=10, decimal_places=2)
class Invoice(models.Model):
    account = models.ForeignKey(Account, on_delete=models.CASCADE)
    amount = models.DecimalField(max_digits=10, decimal_places=2)
    date = models.DateField()
class Purchase(models.Model):
    item = models.CharField(max_length=255)
    amount = models.DecimalField(max_digits=10, decimal_places=2)
    date = models.DateField()
class InventoryItem(models.Model):
    name = models.CharField(max_length=255)
    quantity = models.IntegerField()
class FinancialReport(models.Model):
    title = models.CharField(max_length=255)
    content = models.TextField()
class UserRole(models.Model):
    user = models.ForeignKey(User, on_delete=models.CASCADE)
    role_name = models.CharField(max_length=255)
```

views.py
```python
'''
Handles HTTP requests and responses for the accounting system.
'''
from django.shortcuts import render
from rest_framework import viewsets, permissions
from .models import Account, Invoice, Purchase, InventoryItem, FinancialReport, UserRole
from .serializers import AccountSerializer, InvoiceSerializer, PurchaseSerializer, InventoryItemSerializer, FinancialReportSerializer, UserRoleSerializer
from rest_framework.permissions import BasePermission
class IsAccountManager(BasePermission):
    def has_permission(self, request, view):
        return request.user.userrole_set.filter(role_name='Account Manager').exists()
class IsInvoiceManager(BasePermission):
    def has_permission(self, request, view):
        return request.user.userrole_set.filter(role_name='Invoice Manager').exists()
class IsPurchaseManager(BasePermission):
    def has_permission(self, request, view):
        return request.user.userrole_set.filter(role_name='Purchase Manager').exists()
class IsInventoryManager(BasePermission):
    def has_permission(self, request, view):
        return request.user.userrole_set.filter(role_name='Inventory Manager').exists()
class IsReportManager(BasePermission):
    def has_permission(self, request, view):
        return request.user.userrole_set.filter(role_name='Report Manager').exists()
class AccountViewSet(viewsets.ModelViewSet):
    queryset = Account.objects.all()
    serializer_class = AccountSerializer
    permission_classes = [permissions.IsAuthenticated, IsAccountManager]
class InvoiceViewSet(viewsets.ModelViewSet):
    queryset = Invoice.objects.all()
    serializer_class = InvoiceSerializer
    permission_classes = [permissions.IsAuthenticated, IsInvoiceManager]
class PurchaseViewSet(viewsets.ModelViewSet):
    queryset = Purchase.objects.all()
    serializer_class = PurchaseSerializer
    permission_classes = [permissions.IsAuthenticated, IsPurchaseManager]
class InventoryItemViewSet(viewsets.ModelViewSet):
    queryset = InventoryItem.objects.all()
    serializer_class = InventoryItemSerializer
    permission_classes = [permissions.IsAuthenticated, IsInventoryManager]
class FinancialReportViewSet(viewsets.ModelViewSet):
    queryset = FinancialReport.objects.all()
    serializer_class = FinancialReportSerializer
    permission_classes = [permissions.IsAuthenticated, IsReportManager]
class UserRoleViewSet(viewsets.ModelViewSet):
    queryset = UserRole.objects.all()
    serializer_class = UserRoleSerializer
    permission_classes = [permissions.IsAuthenticated]
```

serializers.py
```python
'''
Serializes the models for the accounting system.
'''
from rest_framework import serializers
from .models import Account, Invoice, Purchase, InventoryItem, FinancialReport, UserRole
class AccountSerializer(serializers.ModelSerializer):
    class Meta:
        model = Account
        fields = '__all__'
class InvoiceSerializer(serializers.ModelSerializer):
    class Meta:
        model = Invoice
        fields = '__all__'
class PurchaseSerializer(serializers.ModelSerializer):
    class Meta:
        model = Purchase
        fields = '__all__'
class InventoryItemSerializer(serializers.ModelSerializer):
    class Meta:
        model = InventoryItem
        fields = '__all__'
class FinancialReportSerializer(serializers.ModelSerializer):
    class Meta:
        model = FinancialReport
        fields = '__all__'
class UserRoleSerializer(serializers.ModelSerializer):
    class Meta:
        model = UserRole
        fields = '__all__'
```

urls.py
```python
'''
Defines URL routing for the accounting system.
'''
from django.urls import path, include
from rest_framework.routers import DefaultRouter
from .views import AccountViewSet, InvoiceViewSet, PurchaseViewSet, InventoryItemViewSet, FinancialReportViewSet, UserRoleViewSet
router = DefaultRouter()
router.register(r'accounts', AccountViewSet)
router.register(r'invoices', InvoiceViewSet)
router.register(r'purchases', PurchaseViewSet)
router.register(r'inventory', InventoryItemViewSet)
router.register(r'reports', FinancialReportViewSet)
router.register(r'userroles', UserRoleViewSet)
urlpatterns = [
    path('', include(router.urls)),
]
```

app.js
```js
'''
Main entry point for the React application.
'''
import React from 'react';
import { BrowserRouter as Router, Route, Switch } from 'react-router-dom';
import AccountComponent from './components/AccountComponent';
import InvoiceComponent from './components/InvoiceComponent';
import PurchaseComponent from './components/PurchaseComponent';
import InventoryComponent from './components/InventoryComponent';
import ReportComponent from './components/ReportComponent';
import UserRoleComponent from './components/UserRoleComponent';
function App() {
  return (
    <Router>
      <Switch>
        <Route path="/accounts" component={AccountComponent} />
        <Route path="/invoices" component={InvoiceComponent} />
        <Route path="/purchases" component={PurchaseComponent} />
        <Route path="/inventory" component={InventoryComponent} />
        <Route path="/reports" component={ReportComponent} />
        <Route path="/userroles" component={UserRoleComponent} />
      </Switch>
    </Router>
  );
}
export default App;
```

accountcomponent.js
```js
'''
Component for managing accounts.
'''
import React, { useState, useEffect } from 'react';
import axios from 'axios';
function AccountComponent() {
  const [accounts, setAccounts] = useState([]);
  useEffect(() => {
    axios.get('/api/accounts/')
      .then(response => setAccounts(response.data))
      .catch(error => console.error('Error fetching accounts:', error));
  }, []);
  return (
    <div>
      <h1>Accounts</h1>
      <ul>
        {accounts.map(account => (
          <li key={account.id}>{account.name}: {account.balance}</li>
        ))}
      </ul>
    </div>
  );
}
export default AccountComponent;
```

invoicecomponent.js
```js
'''
Component for managing invoices.
'''
import React, { useState, useEffect } from 'react';
import axios from 'axios';
function InvoiceComponent() {
  const [invoices, setInvoices] = useState([]);
  useEffect(() => {
    axios.get('/api/invoices/')
      .then(response => setInvoices(response.data))
      .catch(error => console.error('Error fetching invoices:', error));
  }, []);
  return (
    <div>
      <h1>Invoices</h1>
      <ul>
        {invoices.map(invoice => (
          <li key={invoice.id}>{invoice.account.name}: {invoice.amount}</li>
        ))}
      </ul>
    </div>
  );
}
export default InvoiceComponent;
```

purchasecomponent.js
```js
'''
Component for managing purchases.
'''
import React, { useState, useEffect } from 'react';
import axios from 'axios';
function PurchaseComponent() {
  const [purchases, setPurchases] = useState([]);
  useEffect(() => {
    axios.get('/api/purchases/')
      .then(response => setPurchases(response.data))
      .catch(error => console.error('Error fetching purchases:', error));
  }, []);
  return (
    <div>
      <h1>Purchases</h1>
      <ul>
        {purchases.map(purchase => (
          <li key={purchase.id}>{purchase.item}: {purchase.amount}</li>
        ))}
      </ul>
    </div>
  );
}
export default PurchaseComponent;
```

```js
'''
Component for managing inventory.

import React, { useState, useEffect } from 'react';
import axios from 'axios';
function InventoryComponent() {
  const [inventory, setInventory] = useState([]);
  useEffect(() => {
    axios.get('/api/inventory/')
      .then(response => setInventory(response.data))
      .catch(error => console.error('Error fetching inventory:', error));
  }, []);
  return (
    <div>
      <h1>Inventory</h1>
      <ul>
        {inventory.map(item => (
          <li key={item.id}>{item.name}: {item.quantity}</li>
        ))}
      </ul>
    </div>
  );
}
export default InventoryComponent;
```

```js
import React, { useState, useEffect } from 'react';

function ReportComponent() {
  const [reports, setReports] = useState([]);
  useEffect(() => {
    axios.get('/api/reports/')
      .then(response => setReports(response.data))
      .catch(error => console.error('Error fetching reports:', error));
  }, []);
  return (
    <div>
      <h1>Financial Reports</h1>
      <ul>
        {reports.map(report => (
          <li key={report.id}>{report.title}</li>
```

```js
  return (
    <div>
```

```
# LangChain

Building applications with LLMs through composability

Looking for the JS/TS version? Check out LangChain.js.

**Production Support:** As you move your LangChains into production, we'd love to offer more comprehensive support.

Please fill out this form and we'll set up a dedicated support Slack channel.

## Quick Install

`pip install langchain`

or

`conda install langchain -c conda-forge`

## 🤔 What is this?

Large language models (LLMs) are emerging as a transformative technology, enabling developers to build applications that they previously could not. However, using these LLMs in isolation is often insufficient for creating a truly powerful app - the real power comes when you can combine them with other sources of computation or knowledge.

This library aims to assist in the development of those types of applications. Common examples of these applications include:

**❓ Question Answering over specific documents**

- Documentation

- End-to-end Example: Question Answering over Notion Database

**🤖 Agents**

- Documentation

- End-to-end Example: GPT+WolframAlpha

## 📖 Documentation

Please see [here](https://python.langchain.com) for full documentation on:

- Getting started (installation, setting up the environment, simple examples)

- How-To examples (demos, integrations, helper functions)

- Reference (full API docs)

- Resources (high-level explanation of core concepts)
```

# Al-Nokhba for Electronics Accounting System

Welcome to the user manual for the Al-Nokhba for Electronics Accounting System. This comprehensive accounting system is designed to help manage general ledger, invoices, purchases, inventory, financial reports, and user roles. The system is built using Django for the backend and React.js for the frontend, with MySQL as the database on an Ubuntu server.

## Main Functions of the Software

### 1. General Ledger Management
- **Accounts**: Manage and track account balances.
- **Invoices**: Create and manage invoices linked to accounts.
- **Purchases**: Record and manage purchase transactions.

### 2. Inventory Management
- **Inventory Items**: Track and manage inventory items and their quantities.

### 3. Financial Reporting
- **Reports**: Generate and view financial reports.

### 4. User Role Management
- **User Roles**: Assign and manage user roles to control access to different parts of the system.

## Installation

### Prerequisites
- **Python**: Ensure Python is installed on your system.
- **Node.js**: Required for running the React frontend.
- **MySQL**: Set up a MySQL database.
- **Ubuntu Server**: The application is designed to run on an Ubuntu server.

### Backend Setup (Django)

1. **Clone the Repository**:
   ```bash
   git clone <repository-url>
   cd <repository-directory>
   ```

2. **Create a Virtual Environment**:
   ```bash
   python3 -m venv env
   source env/bin/activate
   ```

3. **Install Dependencies**:
   ```bash
   pip install -r requirements.txt
   ```

4. **Configure Database**:
   - Update `settings.py` with your MySQL database credentials.

5. **Run Migrations**:
   ```bash
   python manage.py makemigrations
   python manage.py migrate
   ```

6. **Start the Django Server**:
   ```bash
   python manage.py runserver
   ```

### Frontend Setup (React.js)

1. **Navigate to the Frontend Directory**:
   ```bash
   cd frontend
   ```

2. **Install Node.js Dependencies**:
   ```bash
   npm install
   ```

3. **Start the React Development Server**:
   ```bash
   npm start
   ```

## Usage

### Accessing the Application
- Open your web browser and navigate to `http://localhost:8000` to access the Django backend.
- Navigate to `http://localhost:3000` to access the React frontend.

### Managing Accounts
- Navigate to the "Accounts" section to view and manage account balances.

### Managing Invoices
- Go to the "Invoices" section to create and manage invoices.

### Managing Purchases
- Access the "Purchases" section to record and manage purchase transactions.

### Managing Inventory
- Visit the "Inventory" section to track and manage inventory items.

### Generating Financial Reports
- Navigate to the "Reports" section to generate and view financial reports.

### Managing User Roles
- Go to the "User Roles" section to assign and manage user roles.

## Support

For any issues or questions, please contact our support team at support@chatdev.com. We are here to help you make the most of your accounting system.

Thank you for choosing our software to manage your accounting needs!


3. **Start the React Development Server**:
   ```bash
   npm start
   ```

## Usage

### Accessing the Application
- Open your web browser and navigate to `http://localhost:8000` to access the Django backend.
- Navigate to `http://localhost:3000` to access the React frontend.

### Managing Accounts
- Navigate to the "Accounts" section to view and manage account balances.

### Managing Invoices
- Go to the "Invoices" section to create and manage invoices.

### Managing Purchases
- Access the "Purchases" section to record and manage purchase transactions.

### Managing Inventory
- Visit the "Inventory" section to track and manage inventory items.

### Generating Financial Reports
- Navigate to the "Reports" section to generate and view financial reports.

### Managing User Roles
- Go to the "User Roles" section to assign and manage user roles.

## Support

For any issues or questions, please contact our support team at support@chatdev.com. We are here to help you make the most of your accounting system.

Thank you for choosing our software to manage your accounting needs!
